------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

(a) Aircraft  |CESSNA        |172           |29053         |              |              
(b) Engine    |              |              |              |              |              
(c) Propeller |              |              |              |              |              
 
4. Problem Description
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
DURING ANNUAL INSPECTION WHILE RIGGING RUDDER CONTROL SYSTEM, DISCOVERED RUDDER RETURN
SPRINGS SUBSTANTIALLY LIGHTER THAN THE CORRECT SPRINGS.  APPEARED TO BE AUTOMOTIVE
THROTTLE RETURN SPRINGS.  THE RIGGING PROCEDURE DOES NOT INCLUDE A CABLE TENSION SPEC
MANDATING THE USE OF CORRECT SPRINGS FOR PROPER CABLE TENSION & CORRECT RUDDER & NOSEWHEEL
STEERING RESPONSE.  THE SPRINGS THAT WERE INSTALLED APPEARED OK UNTIL RIGGING WAS
ATTEMPTED.  UPON CLOSER INSP, DISCOVERED THE SPRINGS WERE INCORRECT.  THE DIFFERENCE WAS
ONLY NOTICEABLE WHEN SPRINGS WERE LOOKED AT SIDE-BY-SIDE.  DECEPTIVE APPEARANCE OF THE
BOGUS SPRINGS APPARENTLY FOOLED INSPECTORS FOR YEARS.

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

(b) Engine    |              |              |              |              |              
(c) Propeller |              |              |              |              |              
 
4. Problem Description
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ALL SIX RIVETS HOLDING ELEVATOR TUBE TO FLANGE WERE SHEARED OFF.  THIS ALLOWED THE LT
ELEVATOR TO MOVE INDEPENDENTLY FROM RT ELEVATOR OR CONTROL WHEEL.  CONDITION WAS
DISCOVERED DURING PRE-FLIGHT INSPECTION.  OWNER WAS TALKED OUT OF FLYING IT IN THIS
CONDITION.  WHEN RT ELEVATOR WAS REMOVED AND CHECKED, MOVEMENT WAS DISCOVERED.  THIS
MOVEMENT WAS VERY SLIGHT AND NOT DETECTABLE ON THE AIRCRAFT.  THE ONLY WAY TO CHECK FOR
THIS IS TO MOVE ELEVATORS UP AND DOWN, OPPOSITE EACH OTHER, AND LOOK FOR MOVEMENT BETWEEN
ELEVATOR TUBE AND FLANGE.  NO MOVEMENT IS ACCEPTABLE.

4. Problem Description
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
PILOT REPORT OF FUEL LEAK FROM SELECTOR. FOUND LEAKAGE PAST SHAFT SEAL. REMOVED SELECTOR
VALVE FOR REPAIR. CCA-1550 DRAIN VALVE WAS INSTALLED IN BOTTOM OF SELECTOR VALVE. WHEN
DRAIN VALVE WAS REMOVED, ORING RETAINING WASHER AT END OF DRAIN VALVE WAS OBSERVED TO BE
CRACKED IN NUMEROUS PLACES AND IN IMMINENT DANGER OF FAILURE. HAD THE WASHER BROKEN OFF,
AN UNCONTROLLABLE LOSS OF FUEL THROUGH THE DRAIN VALVE WOULD HAVE OCCURRED. THE ONLY WAY
TO PREVENT FUEL LEAKAGE WOULD HAVE BEEN TO SHUT OFF THE FUEL SELECTOR, WHICH RESULTS IN
ENGINE STOPPAGE.

(c) Propeller |              |              |              |              |              
 
4. Problem Description
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
APPROXIMATELY 20 HOURS AFTER ANNUAL, THE VERNIER MIXTURE CONTROL BECAME VERY STIFF.  THERE
WERE NO KNOWN ANOMALIES OR WEAR NOTED AT THE ANNUAL.  DUE TO THE AGE OF THE PART, IT WAS
REPLACED.  UPON, DISASSEMBLY THE VERNIER PART OF THE CONTROL APPEARED TO STILL WORK
APPROPRIATELY, BUT THERE APPEARED TO BE A LARGE AMOUNT OF BLACK MATERIAL THAT HAD BUILT UP
ON THE LENGTH OF THE CABLE (ESPECIALLY NEAR THE TOP OF THE CABLE ASSEMBLE, NEAR THE TOP OF
THE VERNIER CONTROL).  THE CABLE APPEARED TO BE GUMMY IN NATURE.  UPON POLLING OWNERS,
SOME OWNERS MAY HAVE USED SANITIZER THAT INCLUDED PHENOLS AND/OR METHANOL THAT MAY HAVE
BROKEN DOWN THE BLACK PHENOLIC HOUSING OF THE VERNIER MIXTURE.  A LIGHT LOCALIZED CLEANING
REMOVED THE RESIDUE AND APPEARED TO BE INCONSISTENT WITH DIRT.
